  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_e5544151-b14e-4125-a4a7-2324306e5637'
      });

      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer11123032869670687659"><i>Vikas Swarup's</i> spectacular debut novel opens in a jail cell in Mumbai, India, where Ram Mohammad Thomas is being held after correctly answering all twelve questions on India's biggest quiz show, Who Will Win a Billion? It is hard to believe that a poor orphan who has never read a newspaper or gone to school could win such a contest. But through a series of exhilarating tal</span>
  <span id="freeText11123032869670687659" style="display:none"><i>Vikas Swarup's</i> spectacular debut novel opens in a jail cell in Mumbai, India, where Ram Mohammad Thomas is being held after correctly answering all twelve questions on India's biggest quiz show, Who Will Win a Billion? It is hard to believe that a poor orphan who has never read a newspaper or gone to school could win such a contest. But through a series of exhilarating tales Ram explains to his lawyer how episodes in his life gave him the answer to each question.<br /><br />Ram takes us on an amazing review of his own history - from the day he was found as a baby in the clothes donation box of a Delhi church to his employment by a faded Bollywood star to his adventure with a security-crazed Australian army colonel to his career as an overly creative tour guide at the Taj Mahal.<br /><br /><i>Vikas Swarup's Q &amp; A</i> is a beguiling blend of high comedy, drama, and romance that reveals how we know what we know - not just about trivia, but about life itself. Cutting across humanity in all its squalor and glory, <i>Vikas Swarup</i> presents a kaleidoscopic vision of the struggle between good and evil - and what happens when one boy has no other choice in life but to survive.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11123032869670687659" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/26190129-abby-james"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1433641709i/26190129._UX100_CR0,8,100,100_.jpg" /></a>

<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/26190129-abby-james">Abby James</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I really have to admire the way the screen writer created a whole new story and only loosely based it on the book (just the premise and a few other th<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I really have to admire the way the screen writer created a whole new story and only loosely based it on the book (just the premise and a few other things). It's rare that an interpretation is so well thought out. The book is simple and interesting on its own. The twist at the end is delicious and it was a compelling read. The movie on the other hand had so many layers. It was if it was a completely different novel in itself. Both can be appreciated. :)<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12765387490998974396">Q & A = Slumdog Millionaire, Vikas Swarup<br/><br/>Q & A is a novel by Vikas Swarup, an Indian diplomat. Published in 2005, it was the author's first novel. Set in India, it tells the rags to riches story of Ram Mohammad Thomas, a young waiter who becomes the biggest quiz show winner in history, only to be sent to jail on accusations that he cheated. Over the course of the novel, Ram Mohammed Thomas gives flashbacks of his life to explain to the police how he knew the answers to the show's questions - inc</span>
  <span id="freeText12765387490998974396" style="display:none">Q &amp; A = Slumdog Millionaire, Vikas Swarup<br /><br />Q &amp; A is a novel by Vikas Swarup, an Indian diplomat. Published in 2005, it was the author's first novel. Set in India, it tells the rags to riches story of Ram Mohammad Thomas, a young waiter who becomes the biggest quiz show winner in history, only to be sent to jail on accusations that he cheated. Over the course of the novel, Ram Mohammed Thomas gives flashbacks of his life to explain to the police how he knew the answers to the show's questions - including the corruption he was faced with and had to overcome. <br /><br />The book is about destiny vs luck, and personal dedication. In 2008, the book was loosely adapted into the multiple Oscar-winning movie Slumdog Millionaire, which features a new main character named Jamal and his brother Salim. The movie is a comment on how poverty and corruption poison the human spirit, and how to retain one's true self in the face of adversity.<br /><br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش: روز بیست و ششم ماه نوامبر سال 2010 میلادی<br /><br />عنوان: میلیونر زاغه نشین؛ نویسنده: ویکاس سواروپ؛ مترجم: مهدی غبرایی؛ مصطفی اسلامیه؛ تهران، کتابسرای نیک؛ 1388؛ در 352 ص؛ شابک 9789642953325؛ موضوع: داستانهای نویسندگان هندی به زبان انگلیسی - سده 21 م<br /><br />شرح ماجراهای «رام محمد توماس»، پسر بچه‌ ای كه برای زندگی و زنده ماندن تلاش می‌كند. داستان درباره ی پسر هجده ساله ی یتیم فقیری ساکن «بمبئی»، به‌ نام: «جمال ملک» است، که در مسابقه ی: «چه‌ کسی می‌خواهد میلیونر شود؟»؛ شرکت کرده، و موفق شده تا مرحله ی پایانی، پیش برود؛ همین باعث مظنون‌ شدن پلیس، به تقلب در مسابقه، و دستگیریش می‌شود. بازرس پلیس به او می‌گوید: به‌ شرطی آزادش می‌کند، که بگوید چگونه به پاسخ پرسشها دست پیدا کرده؛ که «جمال» داستان زندگیش را برای مأمور بازجویی بازگو می‌کند. و...؛ ا. شربیانی</span>

<div id="review_49920028" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/49920028" />
    <a title="Megha" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1727205-megha"><img alt="Megha" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1361664925p2/1727205.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/49920028?book_show_action=true">Mar 20, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Megha" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Megha" href="/user/show/1727205-megha">Megha</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781439136652" href="/book/show/5972723-slumdog-millionaire">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1727205-megha?shelf=take-me-home-country-roads">take-me-home-country-roads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1727205-megha?shelf=reviews">reviews</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer49920028" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11898338321820596849"><br/>I should mention that this 1-star review is not at all related to my opinion of the movie <i>"Slumdog Millionaire"</i> which I liked much better than the book. I am glad that the movie-makers smartly retained the only decent thing about this novel that is the game show plot device and tossed almost all of the rest into the trash because that's where this novel truly belongs. This book badly needs some editing or even better, a different author. I read in some review that <i>"Slumdog Millionaire"</i> feels lik</span>
  <span id="freeText11898338321820596849" style="display:none"><br />I should mention that this 1-star review is not at all related to my opinion of the movie <i>"Slumdog Millionaire"</i> which I liked much better than the book. I am glad that the movie-makers smartly retained the only decent thing about this novel that is the game show plot device and tossed almost all of the rest into the trash because that's where this novel truly belongs. This book badly needs some editing or even better, a different author. I read in some review that <i>"Slumdog Millionaire"</i> feels like a juvenile's attempt at writing and I have to agree. It is not even L of literature. It does not take long to get tired of the flat narration. <br /><br />Anyway, writing style is perhaps not the biggest problem with this novel. The story is so full of cliches. Every episode in the life of the protagonist seems as if it is pulled out of some cheap bollywood masala movie (the episodes in the movie Slumdog are way better). Swarup took all the vices and social issues he could think of and stitched it all together into a story. Child abuse, murder, suicide, incest, prostitution, theft, robbery, corruption, eve-teasing, poverty, riots, religious squabbles, underworld, India-Pak war it's all there. Homophobia and pedophilia is way overdone. Such is the cheap drivel Swarup is selling in the name of realism. He has played out the religion card too and named the hero 'Ram Mohammed Thomas'. With this selling recipe in place Mr.Swarup perhaps didn't think there was any need put an effort into the actual writing anymore. <br /><br />These are a few snippets of this book's review from Amazon by people outside India:<br /><br /><i><br />"Despite heartrending descriptions of sexual abuse, racism, poverty, homeless and much, much, more in modern India, this is an utterly enjoyable picaresque adventure that is one of the best reads of the year."<br /><br />"..this is an easy and entertaining story that captures much of the essence of this fascinating country. "<br /><br />"It offers a very good look at several different societies and life-styles in India."<br /><br />"...an exciting and fascinating glimpse into the life in modern India. Well written and full of both common day-life and historical facts about the densely populated peninsula,..."<br /><br />"Gives some overview of reality in India."<br /><br />"...that gives you enough of the misery that exists in India.."<br /><br />"It is well-written and describes India, as it is today."<br /></i><br /><br />Oh, Puhleeze! This ain't modern India (or even India in the older times for that matter). None of the episodes in the book has even a faint resemblance to the life of a common man in India. A common man doesn't spend all his life amidst every imaginable crime and misery. Swarup is pandering to the western audience by giving an impression that abuse, poverty, misery and what not is all there is to Indian way of life. And that too from a person like Vikas Swarup who is an India diplomat and is supposed to represent India to the world outside. At least I think it was pretty clear in the movie that it was just a story of an orphan boy from slums.The depiction of Bombay slum life as a backdrop was perhaps much closer to reality in the movie than Swarup's novel. The movie never seemed to claim that that was the essence of life in India. Swarup, on the other hand, draws his characters from different economic classes, different religions, people ranging from movie stars to diplomats, priests, businessmen, middle-class, slum-dwellers and all. And he presents every possible way of life in India with just a dark side to it.<br /><br />Swarup himself does not even live in India. And even during his visits to India I am sure he has only experienced the life of rich upper class who form only a small fraction of our population. It is not a surprise that he is completely out of the touch of the reality of common life in India. Someone please tell him that watching a bunch of bollywood movies is not how you get an experience of Indian life.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11898338321820596849" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_43494349" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/43494349" />
    <a title="Amy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/764711-amy"><img alt="Amy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1205804660p2/764711.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/43494349?book_show_action=true">Jan 18, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amy" href="/user/show/764711-amy">Amy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781439136652" href="/book/show/5972723-slumdog-millionaire">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/764711-amy?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer43494349" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6634975699264608252">I was completely unenchanted with the movie Slumdog Millionaire; the story, I felt, was predictable with characters that were totally uninteresting or completely unlikable. However, much as I was unimpressed with the movie, I couldn't shake the feeling that there was the kernel of a very interesting story there, and that maybe, just maybe, I might have a good experience with the book.<br/><br/>I am pleased to report that I was correct - the book [u:]Q&A[/u:] is far superior to the film. A few things that </span>
  <span id="freeText6634975699264608252" style="display:none">I was completely unenchanted with the movie Slumdog Millionaire; the story, I felt, was predictable with characters that were totally uninteresting or completely unlikable. However, much as I was unimpressed with the movie, I couldn't shake the feeling that there was the kernel of a very interesting story there, and that maybe, just maybe, I might have a good experience with the book.<br /><br />I am pleased to report that I was correct - the book [u:]Q&amp;A[/u:] is far superior to the film. A few things that I preferred in the novel: <br /><br />1. Not a linear time-frame; in the movie, the progression of questions in Millionaire followed the progress of the boy's life. In the book, this is not the case - the time-line slips around a bit, and answers to certain questions give hints of things not yet revealed that have occurred in the past. It is far more intriguing, I thought, than a simple recitation of "then this happened; then this; and then this."<br /><br />2. Sunil is not a heartless murderer. One of the main problems I had with the film was the Sunil was detestable from the get-go, locking his brother in the toilet, then selling his hard-won autograph. By contrast, the character of Sunil in the novel is a sweet boy, with no relation to the narrator, who loves films, who doesn't kill anyone, and who does not become hardened by the life around him. Sunil from the book is very much what I imagine what they wanted Jamal from the movie to be, except somehow in the movie Jamal was completely lacking in charisma and was actually kind of creepy.<br /><br />3. Minimal love story. I am not a person who is opposed to a love story, certainly; however, as soon as Latika was introduced in the film, I groaned inwardly, that such an interesting premise was being wasted on yet another pair of star-crossed lovers. The book, while there is certainly a romance, it does not span the entire book. Which allows Ram Mohammad Thomas (which is the character of Jamal's name in the book) to develop as a character beyond love-sick obsessive. It also allows the story to develop in interesting ways, as not everything is viewed through the lens of a forlorn lover. There are a lot more characters in the book who get their own stories, with more settings and more things happening. The book creates a believable story of how life experiences can prepare a man to win a billion Rupees on a quiz show that is entertaining, funny, tragic, and horrible, that deserves, rather than is cheapened by, its happy ending. The movie just cannot compare.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6634975699264608252" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1507275106" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1507275106" />
    <a title="Majenta" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50966861-majenta"><img alt="Majenta" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470270651p2/50966861.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1507275106?book_show_action=true">Jan 12, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Majenta" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Majenta" href="/user/show/50966861-majenta">Majenta</a>
      </span>

        rated it

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1507275106" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer8759503182755254348">What's the saying? "You are the sum total of your life's experiences"? This is the book that presents a very young man who has already racked up quite the collection of life experiences, just by experiencing each day of his existence. Luckily and happily, he can put this extraordinary existence to use and win himself a lot of money!<br/><br/>But wait! Here comes yet another unsavory event: he is arrested. For cheating.   <span id="freeText8759503182755254348" style="display:none">What's the saying? "You are the sum total of your life's experiences"? This is the book that presents a very young man who has already racked up quite the collection of life experiences, just by experiencing each day of his existence. Luckily and happily, he can put this extraordinary existence to use and win himself a lot of money!<br /><br />But wait! Here comes yet another unsavory event: he is arrested. For cheating. Nobody can believe that "someone like him" could have known all those answers.<br /><br />They don't know this young man and what his time in this world has been like. They see a dark-skinned, humble peasant. They don't realize that they're looking at someone who could out-survive "Survivor." Someone who is now challenged with getting someone to sit down with him, listen to him, BELIEVE that he is telling the truth.<br /><br />Seize your chance to sit down with him and go Behind the Answers.<br /><br />I loved the chapter names, how the chapters flowed, and getting to know Ram Mohammad Thomas. He endured so much grime, he deserved to have his time to shine!<br /><br />Whatever your opinion of the SLUMDOG MILLIONAIRE film, I humbly suggest that your experience isn't complete without Q &amp; A.<br /><br />Thanks for reading.<br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_719832715" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/719832715" />
    <a title="Sam" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7167549-sam"><img alt="Sam" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1486569910p2/7167549.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/719832715?book_show_action=true">Sep 14, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sam" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sam" href="/user/show/7167549-sam">Sam</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781439136652" href="/book/show/5972723-slumdog-millionaire">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7167549-sam?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer719832715" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4636969189899081629">Vikas Swarup's book is not Danny Boyle's film. I first learned of <i>Q&A</i> from an interview with Swarup, in which he criticized the movie that had made his characters into international names. I can see why.<br/><br/><i>Q&A</i> is an intensely first-person narrative with the details on paper rarely aligning to those that hit celluloid. Swarup leads us into the story through a different scene, plays out the game with different questions, and brings readers to a surprisingly different climax and denouement.<br/><br/>The irony i</span>
  <span id="freeText4636969189899081629" style="display:none">Vikas Swarup's book is not Danny Boyle's film. I first learned of <i>Q&amp;A</i> from an interview with Swarup, in which he criticized the movie that had made his characters into international names. I can see why.<br /><br /><i>Q&amp;A</i> is an intensely first-person narrative with the details on paper rarely aligning to those that hit celluloid. Swarup leads us into the story through a different scene, plays out the game with different questions, and brings readers to a surprisingly different climax and denouement.<br /><br />The irony is that Swarup's version, the original, is almost hopelessly consigned to be the object compared, as relatively few will meet this book before they've seen the movie.<br /><br />Swarup tackles different problems, including gender-based violence and prostitution, that might have tripped up a film rating, but are pulled apart brilliantly by our protagonist, Ram Mohammad Thomas. That's right, not even the names are the same.<br /><br />For all the differences, both book and movie are ultimately strong role models for their format. We hear a much more Indian internal monologue in Swarup's book than in the westernized Boyle voice-over. The language and evolution of Thomas are much less stereotypical than the slumdog, Jamal Malik, that Boyle portrayed.<br /><br />Finding these differences and delighting over each new discovery, in what could have been a mimeograph, is much of the pleasure for someone introduced to Swarup's novel through the cinema. It is a pleasure well worth sampling.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4636969189899081629" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14089957358395976621">I was torn about how to rate this book. On one hand, I just loved the unusual plot, and could have easily given it 5 stars. On the other hand, wow, I don't remember the last time I read anything so blatantly homophobic. Three different male characters, two of whom are clearly identified as "gay", were predatory pedophiles who abused young boys. A third man was also a pedophile who abused young boys, but at least the author never claimed he was gay. I didn't feel any of these characterizations we</span>
  <span id="freeText14089957358395976621" style="display:none">I was torn about how to rate this book. On one hand, I just loved the unusual plot, and could have easily given it 5 stars. On the other hand, wow, I don't remember the last time I read anything so blatantly homophobic. Three different male characters, two of whom are clearly identified as "gay", were predatory pedophiles who abused young boys. A third man was also a pedophile who abused young boys, but at least the author never claimed he was gay. I didn't feel any of these characterizations were necessary elements of the plot, either, so they just seemed gratuitous. It's too bad, because this book could have easily made my list of my favourite novels of all time, but the homophobic overtones sort of ruined it for me.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17786288889333290694">My review is based on the audiobook read by Christopher Simpson, who is absolutely outstanding given his vast array of accents and vocal gymnastics. His readings adds an ingredient that would have been sorely missed without him. Having just visited India, I found I was pulled right into the vivid storyline. <br/><br/>I loved the movie but I found the stories in the book far more appealing. It’s originally entitled "Q&A" which is actually the story’s format. I haven’t been teary-eyed over many stories, but</span>
  <span id="freeText17786288889333290694" style="display:none">My review is based on the audiobook read by Christopher Simpson, who is absolutely outstanding given his vast array of accents and vocal gymnastics. His readings adds an ingredient that would have been sorely missed without him. Having just visited India, I found I was pulled right into the vivid storyline. <br /><br />I loved the movie but I found the stories in the book far more appealing. It’s originally entitled "Q&amp;A" which is actually the story’s format. I haven’t been teary-eyed over many stories, but this one really touched my heart. The narrative jumps around a bit, but it all still plays out quite powerfully. The movie is based on the dynamics from this book, but I wish it used a few more of these stories (while politically, I can understand why they didn’t). Ram Mohammad Thomas (Jamal in the movie), is still quite unforgettable. Salim and the host of other good and bad guys and all of their stories will stay with me for a long time. Even the charismatic TV show emcee has important history… I loved it. It’s heavy at times, but a powerful read.<br /></span>

<div id="review_3463320662" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3463320662" />
    <a title="Briar&#39;s Reviews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32054036-briar-s-reviews"><img alt="Briar&#39;s Reviews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1402183274p2/32054036.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3463320662?book_show_action=true">Jul 31, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Briar&#39;s Reviews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Briar&#39;s Reviews" href="/user/show/32054036-briar-s-reviews">Briar&#39;s Reviews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781439136652" href="/book/show/5972723-slumdog-millionaire">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32054036-briar-s-reviews?shelf=drama">drama</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32054036-briar-s-reviews?shelf=guilty-pleasure">guilty-pleasure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32054036-briar-s-reviews?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32054036-briar-s-reviews?shelf=top-books">top-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32054036-briar-s-reviews?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32054036-briar-s-reviews?shelf=one-hit-wonders">one-hit-wonders</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32054036-briar-s-reviews?shelf=inspirational">inspirational</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32054036-briar-s-reviews?shelf=india">india</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32054036-briar-s-reviews?shelf=film-adaption">film-adaption</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3463320662" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3957597865468827408">Slumdog Millionaire is an excellent read that is packed full of drama and intrigue.<br/><br/>I watched the movie years ago when it came out. I wasn't totally sold on it, but promised myself I would eventually read the book. I managed to pick this book up at a charity book shop, and it's been staring at me on my TBR shelf ever since. With COVID going on, I decided to pick up a few more popular books to add to my 2020 read line up.<br/><br/>This book is so good! Vikas Swarup has a unique way of telling this narrative</span>
  <span id="freeText3957597865468827408" style="display:none">Slumdog Millionaire is an excellent read that is packed full of drama and intrigue.<br /><br />I watched the movie years ago when it came out. I wasn't totally sold on it, but promised myself I would eventually read the book. I managed to pick this book up at a charity book shop, and it's been staring at me on my TBR shelf ever since. With COVID going on, I decided to pick up a few more popular books to add to my 2020 read line up.<br /><br />This book is so good! Vikas Swarup has a unique way of telling this narrative, of a man who won the Indian version of Who Wants to Be a Millionaire. His life ends up teaching him almost every answer, and it is heart breaking yet thrilling. Reading about the man's history and all the ways he learned the answers was so cool. The story is woven in a way you get to learn about his life question by question, which just made it way more intriguing.<br /><br />Also, unlike the film, there is almost no romance in this novel. The film is super romance filled, but this one is just a man existing in his life. There's a pinch of romance, but it's definitely not as romantic as the film might have led you to believe.<br /><br />What's also super interesting is that this is loosely based on a real story. The plot and characters is all fictional, based on whatever was going on in Vikas's head when he was writing. But, the fact that someone did win a show like this is real! It's super cool, and I liked that this story took it's own swing at it instead of just following the real story.<br /><br />Overall, it's a great read that is super unique. It's different than my normal read, and it was super refreshing. I highly recommend it if you are looking for an attention grabbing fictional read.<br /><br />Four out of five stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3957597865468827408" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/113980-trin?shelf=indian-lit">indian-lit</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer47345611" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13096727039887148497">Wow. Simon Beaufoy <i>really</i> deserved that Best Adapted Screenplay Oscar. I didn’t think that <i>Slumdog Millionaire</i> was the Best Movie EVAR! as some people seem to, but the book is just awful. Scattered and poorly written, with a narrative that relies on more farfetched coincidences than a cracked-out <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/239579.Charles_Dickens' title='Charles Dickens' rel='nofollow noopener'>Dickens</a> novel, <i>Q&A</i> also manages to make its protagonist completely unsympathetic, and its romance entirely unromantic. Oh, and the whole thing—the first few chapters especially—is cringingly homophobic.</span>
  <span id="freeText13096727039887148497" style="display:none">Wow. Simon Beaufoy <i>really</i> deserved that Best Adapted Screenplay Oscar. I didn’t think that <i>Slumdog Millionaire</i> was the Best Movie EVAR! as some people seem to, but the book is just awful. Scattered and poorly written, with a narrative that relies on more farfetched coincidences than a cracked-out <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/239579.Charles_Dickens" title="Charles Dickens" rel="nofollow noopener">Dickens</a> novel, <i>Q&amp;A</i> also manages to make its protagonist completely unsympathetic, and its romance entirely unromantic. Oh, and the whole thing—the first few chapters especially—is cringingly homophobic. If you loved <i>Slumdog</i>, this will merely taint your appreciation of it. Though I guess it’s interesting to see how the same concept can be taken in two wildly different directions—one that’ll make people hand out Oscars, and one that’ll make them want to mimic Oscar the Grouch.</span>

  <span id="freeText513957820860495466" style="display:none">I saw the movie made from this when it was on at the cinema - Slumdog Millionaire - and I thought it was a clever premise, although overly graphic in some respects. The book is less descriptive of disturbing scenes than the movie was graphic.<br /><br />It was a very interesting read - I liked reading about the different places that Ram Mohammad Thomas lived and worked, and seeing how chance encounters gave him the knowledge to be able to answer 12 random questions on a quiz show - highly unlikely, but still fun to read!</span>

<div id="review_181096007" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/181096007" />
    <a title="Catie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1886642-catie"><img alt="Catie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1385169623p2/1886642.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/181096007?book_show_action=true">Jul 01, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Catie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Catie" href="/user/show/1886642-catie">Catie</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=book-club">book-club</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=read-in-2011">read-in-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=audio">audio</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer181096007" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14554468986221907011">This is one of those rare occasions when I am going to have to say that I like the movie much more than the book. For one, the movie has the absolutely adorable Dev Patel. For two, I think that it was a fantastic decision on the part of Danny Boyle et. al. to edit out the homophobic stereotyping that permeates the beginning of this book.<br/><br/>I’ve only read seventy five pages, so maybe it gets better. I don’t know. This sort of thing tends to bother me quite a bit and I just can’t get past it.<br/><br/>Let’s re</span>
  <span id="freeText14554468986221907011" style="display:none">This is one of those rare occasions when I am going to have to say that I like the movie much more than the book. For one, the movie has the absolutely adorable Dev Patel. For two, I think that it was a fantastic decision on the part of Danny Boyle et. al. to edit out the homophobic stereotyping that permeates the beginning of this book.<br /><br />I’ve only read seventy five pages, so maybe it gets better. I don’t know. This sort of thing tends to bother me quite a bit and I just can’t get past it.<br /><br />Let’s review specifically what has turned me away from finishing this book:<br /><br />1)	In the vignette for the opening question, the hero’s childhood best friend is obsessed with film star Armaan Ali, who has recently been featured in the gossip rags for a very public break up with his co-star. What’s even worse is that those slanderous writers have accused him of homosexual tendencies, which leads the best friend to buy up all the copies of said magazine that he can afford and burn them. The hero tells us that his friend “hates homosexuals” and then goes on to say:<br /><br /><i>”I, too, know of perverts and what they do to unsuspecting boys. In dark halls. In public toilets. In municipal gardens. In juvenile homes."</i><br /><br />2)	As the hero and his BFF are watching Armaan’s latest, a creepy old man sits down next to them, and then proceeds to fondle himself and molest the best friend, prompting the friend to jump up and threaten murder. In a brief moment of clarity, they realize that their attacker is none other than Armaan himself, wearing a fake beard.<br /><br />3)	For the very next vignette, the child hero is living in a church, as the ward of a priest. When a young priest arrives, the hero spies on him and observes homosexual pornography stuffed in his mattress, men dressed in leather and chains (and riding motorcycles!) showing up at all hours of the night, and cocaine use. The young priest cheekily flaunts his behavior and taunts the young hero.<br /><br />4)	About 24 hours after a 15 year old visitor arrives at the church, the hero walks in on the young priest raping him. <br /><br />Now, if you can read all of that and it doesn’t bother you at all, I suggest you pick up this book. Maybe I am overreacting, but this feels too much like blatant stereotyping of homosexuals as perverted pedophiles. It’s the broadcasting of the homophobic belief that homosexual men will “go after” young boys at any opportunity. A belief that, in 1970, 70% of Americans agreed with.(1) In a 2005 survey, only 54% of Americans said that they “would allow gay people to be elementary school teachers.”(1)<br /><br />So, I think that this erroneous belief is still out there, and I don’t intend to support anything that keeps it alive. Now, in fairness, Vikas Swarup has stated that he did not intend for this to be homophobic, but instead highlight the “exploitation of the weak by the strong.”(2) Honestly, I don’t buy that at all. I hope that this review can inform those that, like me, have a very low tolerance for this sort of thing.<br /><br /><u>Perfect Musical Pairing</u><br /><br />Street Sweeper Social Club – <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ZsjgM0b385g" rel="nofollow noopener">Paper Planes</a><br /><br />Sure, Tom Morello is a guitar-playing god, but doesn’t this second rate cover just make you want to listen to the M.I.A. version? Likewise this book just makes me long for the much more intelligent movie.<br /><br /><br />1.	<a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://psychology.ucdavis.edu/rainbow/html/facts_molestation.html">http://psychology.ucdavis.edu/rainbow...</a><br />2.	<a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.thefullwiki.org/Q_%26_A_(novel)">http://www.thefullwiki.org/Q_%26_A_(n...</a><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14554468986221907011" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_588370695" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/588370695" />
    <a title="Abhinav" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10051075-abhinav"><img alt="Abhinav" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1388563530p2/10051075.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/588370695?book_show_action=true">Apr 12, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Abhinav" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Abhinav" href="/user/show/10051075-abhinav">Abhinav</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780552772501" href="/book/show/870989.Q_A">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10051075-abhinav?shelf=humour">humour</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10051075-abhinav?shelf=i-own-a-copy">i-own-a-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10051075-abhinav?shelf=2013-reading-saga">2013-reading-saga</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10051075-abhinav?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10051075-abhinav?shelf=the-cj-library">the-cj-library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10051075-abhinav?shelf=i-own-an-ebook">i-own-an-ebook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10051075-abhinav?shelf=satire">satire</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10051075-abhinav?shelf=semi-favorites">semi-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10051075-abhinav?shelf=popular-fiction">popular-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer588370695" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14802419652542048914">Whoa. I must start by saying that I've surprised myself by reading the last 170 odd pages in just over a couple of hours.<br/><br/>I suppose the premise of 'Q&A' is known to everyone who hasn't been living under a rock, having been adapted into the Oscar-winning motion picture 'Slumdog Millionaire' in 2008. But that's pretty much where the resemblance ends, because the film takes very little inspiration from the events that take place in the book, which is not necessarily a bad thing.<br/><br/>I say this because I </span>
  <span id="freeText14802419652542048914" style="display:none">Whoa. I must start by saying that I've surprised myself by reading the last 170 odd pages in just over a couple of hours.<br /><br />I suppose the premise of 'Q&amp;A' is known to everyone who hasn't been living under a rock, having been adapted into the Oscar-winning motion picture 'Slumdog Millionaire' in 2008. But that's pretty much where the resemblance ends, because the film takes very little inspiration from the events that take place in the book, which is not necessarily a bad thing.<br /><br />I say this because I have no doubt that Danny Boyle's film is far more realistic &amp; convincing. Swarup's novel is obviously flawed &amp; has its shortcomings, but that shouldn't take away anything from the credible effort he has put into his first novel &amp; he retells the age-old tale of the triumph of the perennial underdog in the modern backdrop of a popular quiz show.<br /><br />I particularly liked the style of narration - how it switches effectively between non-linear narration in flashback mode at the start of every chapter &amp; reverts to the present tense towards the end as the protagonist Ram Mohammad Thomas (shades of 'Life of Pi' in his name) goes on to explain how he happens to know the answer to every question he's asked in the game show.<br /><br />Characterisation is not the strongest point of this novel, given one might happen to lose count of the different characters introduced throughout on account of Ram's numerous experiences. It's not that bad either but none of the characters apart from the protagonist leave much of an impression upon the mind of the reader. But then, one might end up ignoring that because there's just so much happening in Ram's life in the meantime.<br /><br />I thought the ending was too 'filmi' (Bollywood term for 'cliche') for my tastes with the reunion thing &amp; the tiny bit about Ram's lucky coin (obviously inspired from 'Sholay'), but I managed to digest that somewhat. Guess some of us Indians are used to that by now.<br /><br />Engrossing, gripping &amp; with its heart in the right place, I rate Vikas Swarup's debut novel 'Q&amp;A' 4 out of 5 stars simply for its immense entertainment value. It definitely makes for an enjoyable read, besides giving us a rather vivid &amp; colourful version of modern India. Highly recommended for fans of Indian popular fiction.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14802419652542048914" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2189890585?book_show_action=true">Nov 20, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David Rose" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David Rose" href="/user/show/30533345-david-rose">David Rose</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2189890585" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8851876552356898113">I came late to the party - very late. Fortunately I'd not seen the film either (still haven't, but now I hope to), so my impressions of the book are untainted and without any movie-derived preconceptions.<br/><br/>The book is cleverly constructed and offers a whirling kaleidoscope of the India a tourist never sees, except for the Taj Mahal - and then you get an unregistered guide's perspective. From the tragedy and the despair of sprawling slums, to the cheek by jowl living in a chawl, to the darting touc</span>
  <span id="freeText8851876552356898113" style="display:none">I came late to the party - very late. Fortunately I'd not seen the film either (still haven't, but now I hope to), so my impressions of the book are untainted and without any movie-derived preconceptions.<br /><br />The book is cleverly constructed and offers a whirling kaleidoscope of the India a tourist never sees, except for the Taj Mahal - and then you get an unregistered guide's perspective. From the tragedy and the despair of sprawling slums, to the cheek by jowl living in a chawl, to the darting touches of ever-optimistic, aspirational India, Vikas Swarup shares his India with the world. For this alone it is an amazing read.<br /><br />I found one or two aspects of the plot a little contrived - but then, we're talking about a plot where the unlikely hero wins a billion rupees on a game show! For the greatest part of the book, however, the story flowed very naturally. The pace is quite quick for such a substantial book, but the structure was, I thought, just a little repetitive. Only a little. There are a couple of great twists.<br /><br />There are moments of hilarity, volumes of excellent social observation, some quiet wit and some heavy-handed puns. By the end, I felt that I'd enjoyed a literary banquet. <br />Be warned, there are some unpleasantly true-to-life passages and pages. To give a list of specific cautions would spoil the book, so I will just say that these parts are not recommended for sensitive readers. There are, however, no detailed sex scenes (not the same thing as *no* sex scenes) and minimal use of foul language.<br />In the end, I call this a wonderful read, which I was unable to put down until I'd finished. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8851876552356898113" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/46402424?book_show_action=true">Feb 15, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Charity" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Charity" href="/user/show/129343-charity">Charity</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780743267489" href="/book/show/3015093-q-a">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer46402424" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2204230977986360100"><i>Q & A</i> is the book that inspired the film <i>Slumdog Millionaire</i>. However, the two bear little to no resemblance to each other, save for the basic premise: an orphan from the slums of India goes on a game show and wins the top prize, but the show's producers think he must have cheated, so the kid tells stories from his life that relay how he knew the answers to the questions. Aside from this bare bones outline, the book and movie are really two <i>entirely</i> different stories made up of almost <i>entirely</i> d</span>
  <span id="freeText2204230977986360100" style="display:none"><i>Q &amp; A</i> is the book that inspired the film <i>Slumdog Millionaire</i>. However, the two bear little to no resemblance to each other, save for the basic premise: an orphan from the slums of India goes on a game show and wins the top prize, but the show's producers think he must have cheated, so the kid tells stories from his life that relay how he knew the answers to the questions. Aside from this bare bones outline, the book and movie are really two <i>entirely</i> different stories made up of almost <i>entirely</i> different details.<br /><br /><i>Q &amp; A</i> is definitely not for the thin-skinned/weak-stomached. Practically any and every bit of human suffering imaginable is found within its pages: murder, rape, molestation, pedophilia, abuse, child labor, prostitution, suicide, theft, corruption, poverty...the list goes on and on. I was flipping through the pages wondering if the atrocities could actually get worse...they did. Wow! It's almost enough to make you lose faith in humanity.<br /><br />Maybe I'm sick, because I couldn't put it down. I was sucked into the story from the very beginning and each 'chapter' was more powerful than the last. Setting it aside really wasn't an option until I finished the last page. Definitely, a reading experience that I will not soon forget. Amazing!</span>
  <a data-text-id="2204230977986360100" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17939972329551747454">I saw the film a few years ago together with my mother, and I was amazed by the story – almost as much as I was amazed by Dev Patel and how wonderful he is. So, when I learned it was based on a book; it didn't take me long to go to the library in an attempt to find it. However, even though the library claimed to have it, it was nowhere to be found. Until the other day when I found it on a shelf way off where it's supposed to be. Talk about faith.<br/><br/>Ram Mohammad Thomas has just been arrested. Why? F</span>
  <span id="freeText17939972329551747454" style="display:none">I saw the film a few years ago together with my mother, and I was amazed by the story – almost as much as I was amazed by Dev Patel and how wonderful he is. So, when I learned it was based on a book; it didn't take me long to go to the library in an attempt to find it. However, even though the library claimed to have it, it was nowhere to be found. Until the other day when I found it on a shelf way off where it's supposed to be. Talk about faith.<br /><br />Ram Mohammad Thomas has just been arrested. Why? For winning the top prize on India's most popular quiz show. As a boy living in the slums of Mumbai, the producers of the show are convinced he cheated in order to win the billion rupees. Because how else would a slumdog be able to answer all twelve questions correctly? He even said he'd never been to school or even read a newspaper. <br /><br />But when his lawyer asks him to explain how he knows the answers to those twelve questions, he takes her on a wild ride consisting of stories from different periods in his life, from the day he was found abandoned at a church to his days as a tour guide at Taj Mahal to only a few days before the quiz show. Each story contains an explain as to how he could possibly know the answer to each question.<br /><br />Oh god. This is possibly one of the best books I have ever read. It's heart-warming, occasionally hilarious but also heart-wrenching and tragedic. It's an absurd but still realistic story about the life of a young orphan boy and his experiences and relationship as he tries to survive in a world that couldn't care less for him.<br /><br />I didn't want to put the book down and I felt a pang of sadness when I read the last page. I didn't want it to end but at the same time, I didn't want it to continue either. It's brilliant just the way it is; a whirlwind of different genres – everything from comedy to drama, just like life itself. It is raw and powerful and just amazing.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17939972329551747454" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_38028014" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/38028014" />
    <a title="Dale" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/329383-dale"><img alt="Dale" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1448977473p2/329383.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/38028014?book_show_action=true">Nov 18, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dale" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dale" href="/user/show/329383-dale">Dale</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer38028014&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer38028014" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6803446757726524711">I am a self-avowed suckers for happy endings, even when they are a little contrived or a little too pat. So it's not really surprising that Q&A would hold up well for me, because the whole premise of the book is all about pat contrivances and happy endings. The book opens with the arrest of the narrator, Ram, who has just won a billion rupees on an Indian game show; the producers believe he must have cheated to answer all of the questions correctly. He is rescued from brutal police interrogation</span>
  <span id="freeText6803446757726524711" style="display:none">I am a self-avowed suckers for happy endings, even when they are a little contrived or a little too pat. So it's not really surprising that Q&amp;A would hold up well for me, because the whole premise of the book is all about pat contrivances and happy endings. The book opens with the arrest of the narrator, Ram, who has just won a billion rupees on an Indian game show; the producers believe he must have cheated to answer all of the questions correctly. He is rescued from brutal police interrogation by an altruistic young lawyer who intends to defend him against the cheating charges - all she needs is to understand how he knew the answers. So Ram tells his life story in snippets, focusing on the formative moments of his childhood which happened to give him the information he would be quizzed on in front of a t.v. studio audience. It's a bit of a Picaresque adventure as Ram goes from an orphanage to a rectory to the homes of the wealthy and powerful (as a servant) to a ghetto apartment to the Taj Mahal (as a tour guide) to tending bar in the ghetto. As fate would have it, in each of those places he learns some obscure trivia which comes in miraculously handy on the quiz show. In my mind that's a make-or-break premise - if you can swallow it, you'll really enjoy the book, and if it seems too far-fetched, the book will probably annoy you to no end. I found it to be right up my alley - I like looking for the little connections in life and I could read about how living next to an alcoholic former astronomy professor whose daughter named a kitten after Pluto because Pluto is the smallest planet leads to an illiterate boy knowing which is the smallest planet (but not how many planets there are) all day.<br /><br />The brilliant thing about the book is that the ending has multiple plot twists and revelations of its own, tangential to the central question of whether or not the lawyer will help Ram get his billion rupees the producers are trying to renege on. And those revelations are highly coincidental and unlikely in and of themselves, but with the groundwork the book lays beforehand in making coincidences seem commonplace, it all feels right (if a bit rushed).<br /><br />Most importantly, Ram is a great protagonist, likable and virtuous and very easy to root for, so it's genuinely gratifying to see the stars align for him. Horrific things happen to him and all around him throughout his life, but his story was never too painful to be witness to. And, for a sucker like me, his well-deserved happy ending was sweet reward.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6803446757726524711" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText12985022326682026700" style="display:none">I read this book for a book club meeting last month.<br />I had watched the movie a few years ago and I remember enjoying the story. <br />This is told in sections of Thomas' life. He is explaining how a boy from the slums could answer all the questions to win a billion on a game show. My attention was captured while I tried to guess what the next question was going to be on the game show based on the story that Thomas told. I was usually way off.<br /><br />With how crazy my life has been the last few weeks the short stories made this book easy for me to get through *win*<br />I have to say it was not as inspiring as I had thought it would be. It was sad and dirty and missed the big song number that left you with all the *feel goods* at the end of the movie.<br />This was a strong three star read. It just feels like it kind of fizzled at the end.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12985022326682026700" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_150447378" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/150447378" />
    <a title="The Flooze" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/355739-the-flooze"><img alt="The Flooze" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1599955192p2/355739.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/150447378?book_show_action=true">Feb 24, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="The Flooze" class="user" itemprop="url" name="The Flooze" href="/user/show/355739-the-flooze">The Flooze</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781439136652" href="/book/show/5972723-slumdog-millionaire">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/355739-the-flooze?shelf=vanquished_2013">vanquished_2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/355739-the-flooze?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/355739-the-flooze?shelf=lit-fiction">lit-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer150447378" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9238166939872233128"><b><i>Slumdog Millionaire</i> (<i>Q&A</i>) is not a masterpiece of prose. But it <i>is</i> a startling and thought-provoking story, rife with social commentary.</b><br/><br/>The prologue is engaging, swiftly establishing the ludicrousness of a waiter from the slums winning a quiz show. It <b>deftly highlights the resignation</b> the residents of Dharavi feel towards their lot in life: the inevitability of the police taking you away; the abuses doled out by corrupt officers; the belief that you <b>summon only misfortune if you challenge the so</b></span>
  <span id="freeText9238166939872233128" style="display:none"><b><i>Slumdog Millionaire</i> (<i>Q&amp;A</i>) is not a masterpiece of prose. But it <i>is</i> a startling and thought-provoking story, rife with social commentary.</b><br /><br />The prologue is engaging, swiftly establishing the ludicrousness of a waiter from the slums winning a quiz show. It <b>deftly highlights the resignation</b> the residents of Dharavi feel towards their lot in life: the inevitability of the police taking you away; the abuses doled out by corrupt officers; the belief that you <b>summon only misfortune if you challenge the social divide</b>, if you have the audacity to dream of crossing the barrier between the rich and the poor. <br /><br />This <b>dismal acceptance is a common thread</b> of the novel. A woman thinks death must be exquisite, if the abuse doled out by her lover can be so painful yet so sweet. A group of disabled boys think their life in a Dickensian squat is tolerable as it means food, shelter, and protection from other gangs. A neighbor advises Ram that to reach happiness one must only close his senses and he will no longer have to concern himself with the pain surrounding him. With cultivated ignorance comes peace.<br /><br />This is not advice Ram Mohammad Thomas can tolerate. <br /><br /><b><i>Slumdog Millionaire</i> is a story of an underdog. A boy who rails against injustices, using whatever tools fate provides him. In many ways, he’s a remarkable lead.</b> Ram is confronted with harshness and cruelty at every turn, yet maintains an impressive mindfulness of others and remains open to connectedness. He’s sensitive and empathetic, trusting in the universe without being naïve to its pitfalls. He dares many times to dream of crossing the social divide. But moreso he dreams of staying alive, of connecting, of relieving the burdens of others. <br /><br /><b>Fate and the interconnectedness of all things play an incredibly strong role. The synchronicity of events is of mythical proportions. Swarup’s positioning of the hero often strains belief – unless you are willing to trust in the power of luck and the idea that all things happen for a reason. </b> <br /><br />Calling Ram a hero is apt – and double-sided. In each of his retellings, he shows a fierce desire to protect others. <b>At one point I wondered how much of his ability to be at the Right Place at the Right Time was born of a hero complex.</b> But then I considered his many losses as well as the dialogue within his retellings. There’s a flatness to every conversation – an aspect that irked the crap out of me in the beginning. The <b>dialogue comes across as a translation of meaning, not genuine speech suffused with emotion.</b> There’s also a great deal of telling instead of showing. <br /><br /><b>Perhaps the level tone makes it more credible.</b> This boy is not sensationalist in his memories or in his acts. He’s simply doing the things he perceives need doing and nothing more. <b>If Swarup was flamboyant in his writing, our admiration of Ram’s perseverance might flag. With this flatness, there’s no ego to taint the significance of events.</b> <br /><br />Ram’s ability to connect to so many people is underlined by his name, Ram Mohammad Thomas – so called to please the members of an All Faith Committee. (He jokes that he’s lucky the Sikh member did not come to that day’s meeting, or his name would be even longer.) Throughout the book, we hear of religiously-motivated riots, hate crimes, and vicious mobs. We also hear of Ram’s experiences living in chawls or at a church, where he learns the rudiments of all religions from people living together companionably. <b>Ram himself never adheres to any one faith. He is all and none, connected to individuals not ideologies.</b> <br /><br /><b>Swarup’s conceit of the game show questions evoking deeply significant memories is a sound one.</b> It allows us to bounce with Ram through time and circumstances, offering a <b>well-rounded impression of the character. We become invested</b> in Ram’s life, eager for the missing pieces of his time-line. It’s effective. The wrap-around story of the quiz show itself pales in comparison until the literal and figurative big pay-off.<br /><br /><b>There’s so much more to be considered here:</b> the socio-economic divide; the war between India and Pakistan; the violence born of religious fervor vs. the coexistence of varying groups within the same city; corruption and the abuse of power; deciding whether the author is utterly homophobic; on-screen heroics sparking unrealistic ambitions; Minimally Invasive Education as one of the author’s inspirations; the comparison of the book to the movie. <b>The discussions prompted by this book could be unending. I end this review as I started: Is this novel transcendent in its prose? No. But, damn, will it make you think.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="9238166939872233128" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Anne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/546484-anne"><img alt="Anne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500388520p2/546484.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/8326072?book_show_action=true">Oct 27, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne" href="/user/show/546484-anne">Anne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780552772501" href="/book/show/870989.Q_A">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer8326072" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5120168319593902758">I finished reading Q&A this morning, a thoroughly enjoyable read and a real page-turner. If the film, Slumdog Millionaire, based on this novel is anywhere near as good, then it will be one to watch.<br/><br/> Q&A begins with Ram as the winner of the largest prize in a TV quiz show, he is arrested on the grounds of cheating as nobody believes that a waiter in a restaurant in Mumbai could possibly answer all twelve questions correctly.<br/><br/>The following twelve chapters are based on incidents that have happened i</span>
  <span id="freeText5120168319593902758" style="display:none">I finished reading Q&amp;A this morning, a thoroughly enjoyable read and a real page-turner. If the film, Slumdog Millionaire, based on this novel is anywhere near as good, then it will be one to watch.<br /><br /> Q&amp;A begins with Ram as the winner of the largest prize in a TV quiz show, he is arrested on the grounds of cheating as nobody believes that a waiter in a restaurant in Mumbai could possibly answer all twelve questions correctly.<br /><br />The following twelve chapters are based on incidents that have happened in Ram's short, but very full life. Each incident relates to a question in the quiz. This is a really unique way of writing a novel, but it really works. The events are not in chronological order but each chapter is a suspenseful story of it's own.<br /><br />This is a beguiling blend of high comedy, drama, and romance that reveals how we know what we know — not just about trivia, but about life itself. Looking at humanity in all its squalor and glory, Vikas Swarup presents a vision of the struggle between good and evil — and what happens when one boy has no other choice in life but to survive.<br /><br />An excellent read. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5120168319593902758" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8372939322633929462">An enjoyable book written well and organized beautifully. Having each chapter discuss a part of Ram's life and connecting it to the game show questions make it easy to follow and brings us back from the past to witnesses of the game show. Although the book contains many hardships, it makes you wonder what knowledge can be acquired through living itself along with the wisdom of survival. </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('c4wcengbVQLG7sJ/Xp3GiSlftVAwIzyuUlkRc0PtBozBTlcFWTQJ8AQwNm4s6BOkv852tmAbzUk9fSJllws9uw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('fY29EJPgeKFv8MAMw4q1Jt7Pt8FgxM1fFwOczbo1hX/PT/Zvss8kU60uNB2x/2ALSF50JzD8PLh4J6/bbtO+SA==')})
  }

Sebelas orang anak Melayu Belitong yang luar biasa ini tak menyerah walau keadaan tak bersimpati pada mereka. Tengoklah Lintang, seorang kuli kopra cilik yang genius dan dengan senang hati bersepeda 80 kilometer pulang pergi untuk memuaskan dahaganya akan ilmu—bahkan terkadang hanya untuk menyanyikan Padamu Negeri di akhir jam sekolah. Atau Mahar, seorang pesuruh tukang parut kelapa sekaligus seniman dadakan yang imajinatif, tak logis, kreatif, dan sering diremehkan sahabat-sahabatnya, namun berhasil mengangkat derajat sekolah kampung mereka dalam karnaval 17 Agustus. Dan juga sembilan orang Laskar Pelangi lain yang begitu bersemangat dalam menjalani hidup dan berjuang meraih cita-cita. Selami ironisnya kehidupan mereka, kejujuran pemikiran mereka, indahnya petualangan mereka, dan temukan diri Anda tertawa, menangis, dan tersentuh saat membaca setiap lembarnya. Buku ini dipersembahkan buat mereka yang meyakini the magic of childhood memories, dan khususnya juga buat siapa saja yang masih meyakini adanya pintu keajaiban lain untuk mengubah dunia: Đây là một tác phẩm văn học hiện thực phê phán với nội dung nói về cuộc sống khốn khổ của tầng lớp nông dân Việt Nam đầu thế kỉ 20 dưới ách đô hộ của thực dân Pháp. Tác phẩm xoanh quanh nhân vật chính là chị Dậu và gia đình – một điển hình của cuộc sống bần cùng hóa do sưu cao thuế nặng mà chế độ thực dân áp đặt lên xã hội Việt Nam. Tác phẩm này đã vạch trần bộ mặt tàn ác, bất nhân của xã hội thực dân nửa phong kiến đương thời. Đỉnh điểm của cơn cùng cực là việc chị Dậu phải bán con, khoai và bán cả bầy chó để lấy tiền nộp sưu thuế cho chồng và cảnh chị Dậu chạy ra giữa màn trời đêm tối đen như mực và như cái tiền đồ của chị.\nTắt đèn đã được đưa vào chương trình giáo dục văn học Việt Nam trong sách Ngữ văn 8, tập một (đoạn trích Tức nước vỡ bờ) và đã được điện ảnh Việt Nam chuyển thể thành một bộ phim. Tắt đèn là một tác phẩm mang tính chất của một luận ngữ phê phán chế độ thực dân nửa phong kiến đương thời của thế kỉ 20, tắt đèn là luận văn mang tính nghệ thuật cao góp phần thúc đẩy quá trình nhận thức của xã hội đương đại, nó đúng là tác phẩm hay nhất đương thời làm cho giới nghệ sĩ luôn khó khăn trong việc đả kích chế độ &quot;tư nhân sở hữu&quot;.
